Notes on Citation Practices

Throughout the essay, we have drawn on several major theoretical frameworks:

Constructed Emotion Theory (Barrett, 2017): The foundation for understanding emotions as constructed from core affect plus conceptual categorization, rather than as discrete biological universals.

Predictive Processing (Clark, 2013, 2016; Friston, 2010; Hohwy, 2013): The mechanistic framework explaining how the brain generates predictions about sensory input and updates based on prediction errors.

Core Schemas Theory (Gallagher, 2005; Metzinger, 2003; Graziano, 2013): The identification of foundational structural components (body schema, self-schema, attention schema, spatial schema) that organize conscious experience.

Attention Schema Theory (Graziano, 2013): The specific proposal that consciousness arises from the brain’s model of its own attention, with this model evolved for social purposes.

Developmental Theory (Stern, 1985; Rochat, 2009): Understanding how consciousness emerges through social interaction and self-other differentiation in infancy and childhood.

Theory of Mind Research (Wellman et al., 2001; Frith & Frith, 2006): The capacity to model others’ mental states and how this relates to self-understanding.

Integrated Information Theory (Tononi, 2008; Oizumi et al., 2014): A mathematical framework for consciousness emphasizing integrated information.

Cultural Psychology (Wierzbicka, 1999; Mesquita & Frijda, 1992): Documentation of genuine cultural variation in emotional experience and conceptual systems.

Phenomenological Philosophy (Zahavi, 2014; Gallagher & Zahavi, 2012): Analysis of the structure of subjective experience and intersubjectivity.

Special Acknowledgment of Project Sources

This essay draws extensively on several unpublished project documents that synthesize research across multiple domains:

  • “Consciousness, Emotion, and Social Development: An Integrative Framework” - providing the core synthesis of emotion theory, neuroscience, and development.
  • “Core Schemas in Consciousness Theory: Foundational Structures Analogous to Core Affect” - detailing the schema-based approach to consciousness.
  • “Consciousness as Social-Predictive Substrate: The Emergent Middle Layer Between Biology and Sociology” - developing the social-predictive framework.
  • “Consciousness as Predictive Self-Modeling in Social Context” - explaining the recursive strange loop.
  • “A Review of the Sufficient Conditions for Consciousness” (Coppola, 2025) - providing neuroscientific evidence for subcortical contributions.

These integrative documents themselves cite hundreds of primary sources across neuroscience, psychology, philosophy, anthropology, and developmental science. The reference list above includes the most crucial direct citations while acknowledging that the full scholarly foundation is substantially larger.

The interdisciplinary nature of consciousness studies means we draw on multiple citation traditions (neuroscience, psychology, philosophy, anthropology), which we have attempted to synthesize coherently while respecting disciplinary conventions.

Appendix A: The RSP as a Hierarchical Predictive Coding System

Overview

This appendix formalizes the Recursive Social Prediction (RSP) model as a hierarchical predictive coding system. We specify the generative model at each level, the message-passing dynamics between levels, and the precision-weighting mechanisms that govern attention and learning. The formulation builds on Rao & Ballard (1999), Friston (2005, 2010), and Clark (2013), extending hierarchical predictive coding to encompass affect, schemas, and recursive self-modeling.

A.1 Notation and Definitions

A.1.1 Core Variables

A.1.2 Level Indices

A.1.3 Operators

A.2 The Generative Model

A.2.1 Hierarchical Structure

Symbol Domain Definition
\(t\) \(\mathbb{N}\) Discrete time index
\(\mathbf{x}(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_x}\) Exteroceptive sensory input vector (visual, auditory, tactile, etc.)
\(\mathbf{i}(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_i}\) Interoceptive input vector (visceral, proprioceptive, nociceptive signals)
\(v(t)\) \([-1, 1]\) Valence dimension of core affect (unpleasant → pleasant)
\(\alpha(t)\) \([0, 1]\) Arousal dimension of core affect (calm → activated)
\(\mathbf{a}(t)\) \([-1,1] \times [0,1]\) Core affect vector \(\mathbf{a}(t) = (v(t), \alpha(t))\)
\(\mathcal{S}\) — Set of core schemas \(\{s_{\text{body}}, s_{\text{spatial}}, s_{\text{aff-hom}}, s_{\text{attn}}, s_{\text{self}}\}\)
\(\mathbf{s}_k(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_k}\) State vector of schema \(k \in \mathcal{S}\)
\(\mathbf{z}(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_z}\) Integrated schema representation (structured affect)
\(\mathcal{C}\) — Set of available conceptual categories (culturally learned)
\(c^*(t)\) \(\mathcal{C}\) Selected concept maximizing posterior probability
\(\mathbf{e}(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_e}\) Constituted experience (meaningful integration of \(\mathbf{z}(t)\) with \(c^*(t)\))
\(\mathcal{M}(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_m}\) Self-model state vector at time \(t\)
\(\mathcal{O}\) — Set of other-agent models \(\{o_1, o_2, \ldots, o_K\}\)
\(o_j(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_o}\) Model of other agent \(j\)'s mental state
\(\hat{\mathcal{M}}_j(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_m}\) Predicted self-as-seen-by agent \(j\)
\(\hat{\mathbf{e}}(t+1)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_e}\) Predicted future experience
\(\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_l}\) Prediction error at level \(l\)
\(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_l \times n_l}\) Precision matrix at level \(l\) (inverse covariance of prediction errors)
\(\boldsymbol{\Sigma}_l\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_l \times n_l}\) Temporal transition noise covariance at level \(l\)
\(\boldsymbol{\eta}_l(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_l}\) Temporal prediction error: \(\boldsymbol{\mu}_l(t) - f_l(\boldsymbol{\mu}_l(t-1), \boldsymbol{\mu}_{l+1}(t-1))\)
\(\boldsymbol{\xi}_l(t)\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_l}\) Precision-weighted prediction error: \(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l \cdot \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l\)
\(\Phi(t)\) — Phenomenal state: the integrated tuple \(\langle \mathbf{e}(t), \mathcal{M}(t), \hat{\mathbf{e}}(t+1) \rangle\)
Level Label Generative Model Primary Substrate
\(l = 1\) Core Affect \(g_1(\boldsymbol{\mu}_2)\): predicts interoceptive signals from schema states Brainstem, hypothalamus, amygdala, anterior insula
\(l = 2\) Core Schemas \(g_2(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3)\): predicts schema configurations from conceptual/self-model states Somatosensory, hippocampal, frontoparietal, TPJ circuits
\(l = 3\) Recursive Social Prediction \(g_3(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3^{\text{rec}})\): predicts experience from recursive self-model mPFC, TPJ/STS, dlPFC, default mode network
Operator Definition
\(g_l(\cdot)\) Generative function at level \(l\): maps higher-level representations to predictions about the level below
\(f_l(\cdot)\) State transition function at level \(l\): governs temporal dynamics of level-\(l\) representations
\(\boldsymbol{\mu}_l(t)\) Sufficient statistics (expectations) of the approximate posterior at level \(l\)
\(\dot{\boldsymbol{\mu}}_l(t)\) Rate of change of expectations at level \(l\) (gradient descent on free energy)
\(D\) Temporal derivative operator: \(D\boldsymbol{\mu} = \dot{\boldsymbol{\mu}}\)

The RSP generative model is a three-level hierarchy. Each level \(l\) generates predictions about the level below via a nonlinear mapping \(g_l\), with additive Gaussian noise scaled by precision \(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l\):

$$\text{Level 1:} \quad \mathbf{i}(t) = g_1(\boldsymbol{\mu}_2(t)) + \boldsymbol{\Pi}_1^{-1/2} \boldsymbol{\omega}_1$$
$$\text{Level 2:} \quad \boldsymbol{\mu}_1(t) = g_2(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3(t)) + \boldsymbol{\Pi}_2^{-1/2} \boldsymbol{\omega}_2$$
$$\text{Level 3:} \quad \boldsymbol{\mu}_2(t) = g_3(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3^{\text{rec}}(t)) + \boldsymbol{\Pi}_3^{-1/2} \boldsymbol{\omega}_3$$

where \(\boldsymbol{\omega}_l \sim \mathcal{N}(0, \mathbf{I})\) and \(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3^{\text{rec}}\) denotes the recursively updated self-model (see §A.4).

A.2.2 Prediction Errors

At each level, prediction errors encode the discrepancy between actual input and top-down prediction:

$$\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_1(t) = \mathbf{i}(t) - g_1(\boldsymbol{\mu}_2(t))$$
$$\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_2(t) = \boldsymbol{\mu}_1(t) - g_2(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3(t))$$
$$\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_3(t) = \boldsymbol{\mu}_2(t) - g_3(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3^{\text{rec}}(t))$$

These errors are precision-weighted before propagating upward:

$$\boldsymbol{\xi}_l(t) = \boldsymbol{\Pi}_l(t) \cdot \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l(t)$$

where \(\boldsymbol{\xi}_l\) is the precision-weighted prediction error at level \(l\).

A.2.3 Temporal Dynamics

Each level also generates predictions about its own future state via a state transition model:

$$\boldsymbol{\mu}_l(t+1) = f_l(\boldsymbol{\mu}_l(t), \boldsymbol{\mu}_{l+1}(t)) + \boldsymbol{\Sigma}_l^{1/2} \boldsymbol{\nu}_l$$

where \(\boldsymbol{\Sigma}_l\) is the temporal transition noise covariance and \(\boldsymbol{\nu}_l \sim \mathcal{N}(0, \mathbf{I})\).

A.3 Level-Specific Generative Functions

A.3.1 Level 1: Core Affect Generation

The Level 1 generative function maps schema-level expectations to predicted interoceptive states:

$$g_1(\boldsymbol{\mu}_2) = \mathbf{W}_1^{\text{aff}} \, \sigma(\mathbf{z}(t)) + \mathbf{b}_1$$

where:

  • \(\mathbf{W}_1^{\text{aff}} \in \mathbb{R}^{n_i \times n_z}\) is the learned mapping from integrated schemas to interoceptive predictions
  • \(\sigma(\cdot)\) is a nonlinear activation function (e.g., sigmoid or tanh)
  • \(\mathbf{b}_1\) is a bias term encoding homeostatic set-points

The core affect vector is derived from the precision-weighted prediction error:

$$\mathbf{a}(t) = \phi_{\text{aff}}(\boldsymbol{\xi}_1(t))$$

where \(\phi_{\text{aff}}: \mathbb{R}^{n_i} \to [-1,1] \times [0,1]\) is a learned projection onto the valence-arousal plane. Interoceptive prediction errors that signal homeostatic deviation produce negative valence and high arousal; errors consistent with allostasis produce positive valence.

A.3.2 Level 2: Schema Integration

Each schema \(k \in \mathcal{S}\) maintains its own state vector \(\mathbf{s}_k(t)\) updated by both bottom-up sensory input and top-down predictions from Level 3:

$$\mathbf{s}_k(t) = f_k^{\text{schema}}\big(\mathbf{s}_k(t-1), \; \mathbf{x}_k(t), \; \mathbf{a}(t), \; g_{2,k}(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3(t))\big)$$

where:

  • \(\mathbf{x}_k(t)\) is the sensory input relevant to schema \(k\) (e.g., proprioceptive signals for body schema, spatial cues for spatial schema)
  • \(g_{2,k}\) is the Level 3 → schema-\(k\) prediction function
  • \(f_k^{\text{schema}}\) is the schema-specific update function (learned)

The five schemas and their primary inputs:

Schema \(k\) Primary Input \(\mathbf{x}_k\) State \(\mathbf{s}_k\) Encodes
\(s_{\text{body}}\) Proprioceptive, tactile, vestibular Body configuration, boundaries, ownership
\(s_{\text{spatial}}\) Visual-spatial, hippocampal place/grid cells Allocentric and egocentric spatial maps
\(s_{\text{aff-hom}}\) Interoceptive, hypothalamic Homeostatic state, energy balance, drive states
\(s_{\text{attn}}\) Frontoparietal priority maps Attentional focus, salience, awareness attribution
\(s_{\text{self}}\) Mirror system, TPJ, precuneus Self-other distinction, agency, ownership

Schema integration combines individual schema states into a unified structured representation:

$$\mathbf{z}(t) = \text{Integrate}\big(\mathbf{a}(t), \; \{\mathbf{s}_k(t)\}_{k \in \mathcal{S}}\big) = \sigma\left(\mathbf{W}_{\text{int}} \cdot \text{concat}(\mathbf{a}(t), \mathbf{s}_1(t), \ldots, \mathbf{s}_5(t)) + \mathbf{b}_{\text{int}}\right)$$

where \(\mathbf{W}_{\text{int}}\) is a learned integration matrix implementing cross-schema binding.

A.3.3 Level 3: Recursive Social Prediction

Level 3 operates in two stages:

Stage 3a — Conceptual categorization:

$$c^*(t) = \arg\max_{c \in \mathcal{C}} \; P(c \mid \mathbf{z}(t), \; \text{context}(t))$$

The constituted experience is the integration of structured affect with the selected concept:

$$\mathbf{e}(t) = \phi_{\text{exp}}\big(\mathbf{z}(t), \; \mathbf{h}_{c^*}\big)$$

where \(\mathbf{h}_{c^*} \in \mathbb{R}^{n_c}\) is the learned embedding of concept \(c^*\).

Stage 3b — Recursive self-modeling (see §A.4 for full specification).

A.4 The Recursive Self-Model

A.4.1 Self-Model Update

The self-model \(\mathcal{M}(t)\) is updated by integrating the current constituted experience:

$$\mathcal{M}(t) = f_{\mathcal{M}}\big(\mathcal{M}(t-1), \; \mathbf{e}(t)\big) = \mathcal{M}(t-1) + \lambda_{\mathcal{M}} \cdot \tanh\big(\mathbf{W}_{\mathcal{M}} \cdot [\mathcal{M}(t-1); \mathbf{e}(t)] + \mathbf{b}_{\mathcal{M}}\big)$$

where \(\lambda_{\mathcal{M}} \in (0, 1]\) is the self-model learning rate and \([\cdot;\cdot]\) denotes concatenation.

A.4.2 Other-Model Maintenance

For each agent \(j\) in the social context \(\mathcal{O}\):

$$o_j(t) = f_o\big(o_j(t-1), \; \mathbf{x}_j^{\text{social}}(t)\big)$$

where \(\mathbf{x}_j^{\text{social}}(t)\) encodes observed behavior, facial expressions, vocal prosody, and inferred intentions of agent \(j\).

A.4.3 The Strange Loop: Recursive Depth

For recursion depth \(d = 1, \ldots, D_{\max}\):

$$\hat{\mathcal{M}}_j^{(d)}(t) = \text{PredictSelfAsSeenBy}\big(\mathcal{M}^{(d-1)}(t), \; o_j(t)\big)$$
$$\hat{\mathcal{M}}^{(d)}(t) = \sum_{j=1}^{|\mathcal{O}|} w_j \cdot \hat{\mathcal{M}}_j^{(d)}(t)$$
$$\mathcal{M}^{(d)}(t) = (1 - \beta_d) \cdot \mathcal{M}^{(d-1)}(t) + \beta_d \cdot \hat{\mathcal{M}}^{(d)}(t)$$

where:

  • \(\mathcal{M}^{(0)}(t) = \mathcal{M}(t)\) after the Stage 3a update
  • \(w_j \in [0,1]\) are salience weights for each other-agent (\(\sum_j w_j = 1\))
  • \(\beta_d \in (0, 1)\) is a depth-dependent mixing coefficient, typically \(\beta_d = \beta_0 \cdot \gamma^d\) with decay \(\gamma \in (0,1)\), ensuring deeper recursion has diminishing influence

The final self-model after \(D_{\max}\) recursion steps is:

$$\boldsymbol{\mu}_3^{\text{rec}}(t) = \mathcal{M}^{(D_{\max})}(t)$$

A.4.4 Recursion Depth and Convergence

The recursion terminates when either \(d = D_{\max}\) or the update magnitude falls below threshold:

$$\|\mathcal{M}^{(d)}(t) - \mathcal{M}^{(d-1)}(t)\| < \delta_{\text{conv}}$$

Typical biological values: \(D_{\max} \approx 3\text{–}5\) (corresponding to the depth of recursive mentalizing observed empirically: "I think that you think that I think..."), \(\delta_{\text{conv}} \approx 0.01\).

A.5 Message Passing Dynamics

A.5.1 Bottom-Up: Precision-Weighted Prediction Errors

Prediction errors propagate upward, weighted by precision:

$$\boldsymbol{\xi}_l(t) = \boldsymbol{\Pi}_l(t) \cdot \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l(t) \quad \text{(upward message from level } l \text{)}$$

A.5.2 Top-Down: Predictions

Predictions propagate downward via the generative functions:

$$\hat{\boldsymbol{\mu}}_{l-1}(t) = g_l(\boldsymbol{\mu}_l(t)) \quad \text{(downward message from level } l \text{)}$$

A.5.3 Expectation Update (Gradient Descent on Free Energy)

At each level, expectations are updated by gradient descent on variational free energy (see Appendix B):

$$\dot{\boldsymbol{\mu}}_l = D\boldsymbol{\mu}_l - \kappa_l \cdot \frac{\partial F}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_l}$$

Expanding the free energy gradient (omitting temporal terms for clarity; see Appendix B, §B.4.1 for the full expansion):

$$\frac{\partial F}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_l} = -\frac{\partial g_{l-1}^T}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_l} \boldsymbol{\xi}_{l-1} + \boldsymbol{\xi}_{l+1}$$

where \(g_{l-1}(\boldsymbol{\mu}_l)\) is the generative function that takes \(\boldsymbol{\mu}_l\) as input to predict the level below:

  • The first term drives expectations toward explaining bottom-up prediction errors (via the Jacobian of the generative function that maps from level \(l\))
  • The second term ensures consistency with top-down predictions from the level above (\(\boldsymbol{\mu}_l\) enters linearly in \(\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_{l+1}\), so no Jacobian is needed)
  • \(\kappa_l > 0\) is the learning rate at level \(l\)

A.5.4 Precision Update

Precisions are themselves updated to minimize free energy:

$$\dot{\boldsymbol{\Pi}}_l = -\eta_l \cdot \frac{\partial F}{\partial \boldsymbol{\Pi}_l} = \eta_l \left(\frac{1}{2}\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l^{-1} - \frac{1}{2}\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l^T\right)$$

This implements attention: high precision at a level means prediction errors there are weighted more heavily, driving the system to explain those errors. The attention schema (\(s_{\text{attn}}\)) modulates \(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l\) across levels, implementing the RSP model's claim that attention determines which computations reach consciousness.

A.6 The Phenomenal State

With the dynamics of message passing, expectation update, and precision modulation in hand, we can now characterize what the system's state looks like when these dynamics reach (approximate) convergence — the phenomenal state.

The phenomenal state \(\Phi(t)\) is not a separate output but the integrated state of the hierarchy at convergence:

$$\Phi(t) = \big\langle \mathbf{e}(t), \; \mathcal{M}^{(D_{\max})}(t), \; \hat{\mathbf{e}}(t+1) \big\rangle$$

where:

  • \(\mathbf{e}(t)\) is the constituted experience (what it feels like)
  • \(\mathcal{M}^{(D_{\max})}(t)\) is the recursively refined self-model (who is feeling it)
  • \(\hat{\mathbf{e}}(t+1)\) is the predicted next experience (the forward-looking character of consciousness)

Consciousness, on this account, is the process of hierarchical inference itself — not a separate property generated by the inference, but the inference as experienced from within the system performing it.

A.7 Summary of Information Flow

Interoceptive input i(t) ──→ ε₁ = i(t) - g₁(μ₂) ──→ ξ₁ = Π₁·ε₁ ──→ (upward to Level 2)
                                    ↑
                          g₁(μ₂) ←── (downward from Level 2)

Schema states s_k(t) ──→ ε₂ = μ₁ - g₂(μ₃) ──→ ξ₂ = Π₂·ε₂ ──→ (upward to Level 3)
                                    ↑
                          g₂(μ₃) ←── (downward from Level 3)

Self-model M(t) ──→ ε₃ = μ₂ - g₃(M^rec) ──→ ξ₃ = Π₃·ε₃ ──→ (recursive update)
                                    ↑
                          g₃(M^rec) ←── (strange loop recursion)

Each level simultaneously:

  1. Receives precision-weighted prediction errors from below (surprise signal)
  2. Generates predictions downward (expectation signal)
  3. Updates its own expectations to minimize free energy
  4. Updates its precision estimates (attention allocation)

This bidirectional flow, operating continuously, constitutes the stream of consciousness.

References for Appendix A

  • Clark, A. (2013). Whatever next? Predictive brains, situated agents, and the future of cognitive science. Behavioral and Brain Sciences, 36(3), 181-204.
  • Friston, K. (2005). A theory of cortical responses. Philosophical Transactions of the Royal Society B, 360(1456), 815-836.
  • Friston, K. (2010). The free-energy principle: A unified brain theory? Nature Reviews Neuroscience, 11(2), 127-138.
  • Rao, R. P. N., & Ballard, D. H. (1999). Predictive coding in the visual cortex: A functional interpretation of some extra-classical receptive-field effects. Nature Neuroscience, 2(1), 79-87.
  • Seth, A. K. (2013). Interoceptive inference, emotion, and the embodied self. Trends in Cognitive Sciences, 17(11), 565-573.

Appendix B: Free Energy Formulation of RSP

Overview

This appendix derives the variational free energy functional for the Recursive Social Prediction (RSP) model. We show how each level of the hierarchy contributes to a single scalar free energy bound, how minimizing this bound implements perception, learning, and attention, and how the recursive self-model enters as a uniquely self-referential term. The formulation builds on Friston (2005, 2010), Buckley et al. (2017), and Bogacz (2017), extending variational inference to encompass affect, schemas, and recursive social prediction.

Notation. All symbols follow Appendix A. In particular: \(\boldsymbol{\mu}_l\) denotes expectations at level \(l\); \(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l\) denotes precision matrices; \(g_l(\cdot)\) denotes generative functions; \(\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l = \text{input}_l - g_l(\boldsymbol{\mu}_{l+1})\) denotes prediction errors.

B.1 The Variational Free Energy Principle

B.1.1 From Bayes to Free Energy

An organism maintains a generative model \(p(\mathbf{y}, \boldsymbol{\theta})\) of sensory observations \(\mathbf{y}\) and hidden causes \(\boldsymbol{\theta}\). Exact Bayesian inference — computing the posterior \(p(\boldsymbol{\theta} \mid \mathbf{y})\) — is intractable for hierarchical nonlinear models. Instead, the system maintains an approximate posterior \(q(\boldsymbol{\theta})\) and minimizes the divergence between this approximation and the true posterior.

The variational free energy is:

$$F = -\ln p(\mathbf{y}) + D_{\text{KL}}\big[q(\boldsymbol{\theta}) \,\|\, p(\boldsymbol{\theta} \mid \mathbf{y})\big]$$

Since \(D_{\text{KL}} \geq 0\), free energy is an upper bound on surprisal:

$$F \geq -\ln p(\mathbf{y}) = \text{surprisal}$$

Minimizing \(F\) with respect to \(q\) tightens this bound, making the approximate posterior approach the true posterior. Minimizing \(F\) with respect to action changes sensory input to reduce surprise.

B.1.2 The Laplace Approximation

Under the Laplace (or "maximum a posteriori") approximation, the approximate posterior is a Gaussian centered on its mode:

$$q(\boldsymbol{\theta}) = \mathcal{N}(\boldsymbol{\mu}, \boldsymbol{\Sigma})$$

where \(\boldsymbol{\mu}\) are the sufficient statistics (expectations) and \(\boldsymbol{\Sigma}\) is the posterior covariance. Under this approximation, the free energy simplifies to an expression involving only prediction errors and precisions (see §B.2).

B.1.3 Definitions

B.2 Free Energy for the RSP Hierarchy

B.2.1 Total Free Energy Decomposition

Symbol Domain Definition
\(F\) \(\mathbb{R}\) Total variational free energy (scalar)
\(F_l\) \(\mathbb{R}\) Free energy contribution from level \(l\)
\(\mathbf{y}\) \(\mathbb{R}^{n_y}\) Complete sensory observation vector \(\mathbf{y} = [\mathbf{x}(t); \mathbf{i}(t)]\)
\(\boldsymbol{\theta}\) — All hidden causes: \(\boldsymbol{\theta} = \{\boldsymbol{\mu}_1, \boldsymbol{\mu}_2, \boldsymbol{\mu}_3, \boldsymbol{\mu}_3^{\text{rec}}\}\)
\(q(\boldsymbol{\theta})\) — Approximate posterior (recognition density)
\(p(\mathbf{y}, \boldsymbol{\theta})\) — Generative model (joint density over observations and causes)
$$D_{\text{KL}}[\cdot \ \cdot]$$ \(\mathbb{R}_{\geq 0}\) Kullback-Leibler divergence
\(\mathcal{L}\) \(\mathbb{R}\) Negative free energy (evidence lower bound, ELBO): \(\mathcal{L} = -F\)

Under the Laplace approximation with Gaussian noise at each level (as specified in Appendix A, §A.2.1), the total free energy decomposes into a sum of level-specific contributions:

$$F = F_1 + F_2 + F_3 + F_{\text{temporal}}$$

Each level contributes a term proportional to the precision-weighted squared prediction error plus a complexity penalty:

$$F_l = \underbrace{\frac{1}{2} \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l^T \boldsymbol{\Pi}_l \, \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l}_{\text{accuracy}} - \underbrace{\frac{1}{2} \ln |\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l|}_{\text{complexity}} + \underbrace{\frac{n_l}{2} \ln(2\pi)}_{\text{constant}}$$

where:

  • \(\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l(t) = \text{input}_l(t) - g_l(\boldsymbol{\mu}_{l+1}(t))\) is the prediction error at level \(l\)
  • \(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l(t)\) is the precision (inverse covariance) of prediction errors
  • \(n_l = \dim(\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l)\) is the dimensionality of level \(l\)
  • The accuracy term penalizes prediction errors proportional to confidence (precision)
  • The complexity term penalizes excessive confidence, preventing overfitting

B.2.2 Temporal Free Energy

The temporal component penalizes deviations from predicted state transitions:

$$F_{\text{temporal}} = \sum_{l=1}^{3} \frac{1}{2} \boldsymbol{\eta}_l^T \boldsymbol{\Sigma}_l^{-1} \boldsymbol{\eta}_l - \frac{1}{2} \ln |\boldsymbol{\Sigma}_l^{-1}| + \frac{n_l}{2} \ln(2\pi)$$

where \(\boldsymbol{\eta}_l(t) = \boldsymbol{\mu}_l(t) - f_l(\boldsymbol{\mu}_l(t-1), \boldsymbol{\mu}_{l+1}(t-1))\) is the temporal prediction error — the discrepancy between the current state and what the transition model predicted.

B.3 Level-Specific Free Energy

B.3.1 Level 1: Core Affect Free Energy

$$F_1 = \frac{1}{2} \big[\mathbf{i}(t) - g_1(\boldsymbol{\mu}_2)\big]^T \boldsymbol{\Pi}_1 \big[\mathbf{i}(t) - g_1(\boldsymbol{\mu}_2)\big] - \frac{1}{2} \ln |\boldsymbol{\Pi}_1$$

Interpretation. Level 1 free energy is high when interoceptive signals deviate from what the body schema predicts. A racing heart in a safe context produces large \(\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_1\), driving up \(F_1\), which the system resolves by either updating schema expectations (perception: "I must be anxious") or changing the body state (action: deep breathing). High \(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_1\) means the system trusts interoceptive signals — interoceptive sensitivity that Seth (2013) links to emotional awareness.

Affective valence as free energy gradient. The core affect vector \(\mathbf{a}(t) = \phi_{\text{aff}}(\boldsymbol{\xi}_1(t))\) can be rewritten in terms of the free energy gradient:

$$v(t) \approx -\text{sign}\left(\frac{\partial F_1}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_2}\right) \cdot \left\|\frac{\partial F_1}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_2}\right\$$

Negative valence tracks the direction and magnitude of free energy increase — felt unpleasantness is the phenomenology of rising interoceptive surprise.

B.3.2 Level 2: Schema Free Energy

$$F_2 = \frac{1}{2} \big[\boldsymbol{\mu}_1 - g_2(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3)\big]^T \boldsymbol{\Pi}_2 \big[\boldsymbol{\mu}_1 - g_2(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3)\big] - \frac{1}{2} \ln |\boldsymbol{\Pi}_2$$

The schema-level free energy has a richer structure because \(\boldsymbol{\mu}_1\) is itself a vector of affect-enriched states and \(g_2\) must predict five schema configurations simultaneously. Expanding:

$$F_2 = \sum_{k \in \mathcal{S}} F_{2,k} + F_{2,\text{cross}}$$

where:

$$F_{2,k} = \frac{1}{2} \big[\mathbf{s}_k(t) - g_{2,k}(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3)\big]^T \boldsymbol{\Pi}_{2,k} \big[\mathbf{s}_k(t) - g_{2,k}(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3)\big]$$

is the free energy for schema \(k\), and \(F_{2,\text{cross}}\) captures cross-schema coupling (off-diagonal blocks of \(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_2\)). The five schema-specific terms:

Schema \(F_{2,k}\) Measures Surprise About...
\(s_{\text{body}}\) Body configuration deviating from predicted posture/ownership
\(s_{\text{spatial}}\) Spatial location deviating from predicted navigation state
\(s_{\text{aff-hom}}\) Homeostatic balance deviating from predicted metabolic state
\(s_{\text{attn}}\) Attentional focus deviating from predicted salience map
\(s_{\text{self}}\) Self-other boundary deviating from predicted agency/ownership

Attention as precision optimization. The attention schema \(s_{\text{attn}}\) has a special role: it modulates \(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_{2,k}\) for all other schemas. This means the attention schema's state determines how much weight each schema's prediction errors carry in the total free energy. Formally:

$$\boldsymbol{\Pi}_{2,k}(t) = \boldsymbol{\Pi}_{2,k}^{\text{base}} \cdot \sigma\big(\mathbf{W}_{\text{attn},k} \cdot \mathbf{s}_{\text{attn}}(t)\big)$$

where \(\sigma\) is a sigmoid ensuring positive definite precision. This implements the RSP model's claim that consciousness is determined by which computations receive attentional precision-weighting.

B.3.3 Level 3: Recursive Self-Model Free Energy

$$F_3 = \frac{1}{2} \big[\boldsymbol{\mu}_2 - g_3(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3^{\text{rec}})\big]^T \boldsymbol{\Pi}_3 \big[\boldsymbol{\mu}_2 - g_3(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3^{\text{rec}})\big] - \frac{1}{2} \ln |\boldsymbol{\Pi}_3$$

The self-referential term. Unlike Levels 1 and 2, the hidden cause at Level 3 is the recursively updated self-model \(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3^{\text{rec}} = \mathcal{M}^{(D_{\max})}(t)\). This means the system minimizes surprise about its own schema states as predicted by a model of itself as seen through others' eyes. The free energy is not merely about matching observations to predictions — it is about the self-model's coherence with its social reflections.

Expanding the recursive structure (from Appendix A, §A.4.3):

$$F_3^{\text{rec}} = \sum_{d=1}^{D_{\max}} \gamma^d \cdot \frac{1}{2} \big\|\mathcal{M}^{(d)}(t) - \mathcal{M}^{(d-1)}(t)\big\|_{\boldsymbol{\Pi}_3^{(d)}}^2$$

where:

  • \(\gamma \in (0,1)\) is the recursion discount factor (deeper recursions contribute less)
  • \(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_3^{(d)}\) is the precision at recursion depth \(d\)
  • \(\|\mathbf{x}\|_{\mathbf{A}}^2 = \mathbf{x}^T \mathbf{A} \mathbf{x}\) is the Mahalanobis norm

This sum over recursion depths formalizes the "strange loop": each depth adds a term penalizing the discrepancy between how I see myself and how I predict others see me seeing myself... to depth \(D_{\max}\).

B.4 Gradient Dynamics: Minimizing Free Energy

B.4.1 Expectation Updates

The expectation dynamics at each level follow gradient descent on the total free energy (as stated in Appendix A, §A.5.3):

$$\dot{\boldsymbol{\mu}}_l = D\boldsymbol{\mu}_l - \kappa_l \cdot \frac{\partial F}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_l}$$

We now derive the update direction \(-\frac{\partial F}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_l}\) explicitly for each level (the negative gradient, which is the direction expectations move under gradient descent).

Level 1:

$$-\frac{\partial F}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_1} = -\boldsymbol{\Pi}_2 \cdot \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_2 - \boldsymbol{\Sigma}_1^{-1} \cdot \boldsymbol{\eta}_1$$

The first term drives Level 1 expectations toward the Level 2 prediction (reducing prediction error \(\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_2 = \boldsymbol{\mu}_1 - g_2(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3)\)). The second term enforces temporal consistency (how much Level 1 deviates from its own predicted dynamics).

Level 2:

$$-\frac{\partial F}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_2} = \underbrace{\frac{\partial g_1^T}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_2} \boldsymbol{\Pi}_1 \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_1}_{\text{explain interoceptive errors}} - \underbrace{\boldsymbol{\Pi}_3 \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_3}_{\text{reduce self-model error}} - \underbrace{\boldsymbol{\Sigma}_2^{-1} \boldsymbol{\eta}_2}_{\text{temporal consistency}}$$

Level 2 expectations are simultaneously pulled by three forces:

  1. Downward: adjust schemas to better predict interoceptive signals (via \(g_1\))
  2. Upward: reduce prediction error at Level 3 (since \(\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_3 = \boldsymbol{\mu}_2 - g_3(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3^{\text{rec}})\), the system adjusts \(\boldsymbol{\mu}_2\) toward the self-model's prediction)
  3. Temporal: remain consistent with the transition model's predictions

This multi-directional gradient is the formal expression of the "meaningful integration" that the RSP model claims constitutes experience.

Level 3:

$$-\frac{\partial F}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_3} = \frac{\partial g_2^T}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_3} \boldsymbol{\Pi}_2 \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_2 - \frac{\partial F_3^{\text{rec}}}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_3} - \boldsymbol{\Sigma}_3^{-1} \boldsymbol{\eta}_3$$

The recursive term \(\frac{\partial F_3^{\text{rec}}}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_3}\) is what makes Level 3 uniquely self-referential: the self-model's update depends on the self-model itself, creating a fixed-point problem that the system solves iteratively (the strange loop).

B.4.2 Precision Updates

Precisions are updated by gradient descent on \(F\) with respect to \(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l\) (Appendix A, §A.5.4):

$$\dot{\boldsymbol{\Pi}}_l = -\eta_l \cdot \frac{\partial F}{\partial \boldsymbol{\Pi}_l} = \eta_l \left(\frac{1}{2}\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l^{-1} - \frac{1}{2}\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l^T\right)$$

At equilibrium (\(\dot{\boldsymbol{\Pi}}_l = 0\)):

$$\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l^{*} = \big\langle\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l^T\big\rangle_t^{-1}$$

where \(\langle \cdot \rangle_t\) denotes time-averaging (the instantaneous outer product \(\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_l^T\) is rank-1; the time-averaged empirical covariance is full-rank and invertible). This means the optimal precision equals the inverse of the empirical error covariance — the system learns to trust levels whose prediction errors are small and stable. This is a self-tuning mechanism: levels that predict well gain more influence over the hierarchy.

B.4.3 Action as Free Energy Minimization

The organism can also minimize free energy through action — changing sensory input rather than updating internal states:

$$\dot{\mathbf{u}} = -\kappa_u \cdot \frac{\partial F}{\partial \mathbf{u}} = -\kappa_u \cdot \frac{\partial \mathbf{y}^T}{\partial \mathbf{u}} \boldsymbol{\Pi}_1 \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_1$$

where \(\mathbf{u}(t)\) is the motor command vector and \(\frac{\partial \mathbf{y}}{\partial \mathbf{u}}\) is the (learned) mapping from actions to sensory consequences.

Active inference in the RSP context. The organism doesn't just passively update beliefs — it acts to make its predictions come true. Emotional expression (facial, vocal, postural) is active inference on the interoceptive model: the system predicts a calm body state and acts to bring the body into alignment. Social behavior is active inference on the self-model: the system predicts how others see it and acts to bring social reality into alignment with its self-concept.

B.5 Consciousness as Free Energy Minimization

B.5.1 The Phenomenal State Revisited

The phenomenal state \(\Phi(t) = \langle \mathbf{e}(t), \mathcal{M}^{(D_{\max})}(t), \hat{\mathbf{e}}(t+1) \rangle\) is the state of the hierarchy at the point where free energy is (locally) minimized. Consciousness, on this account, is not a reward for minimizing free energy — it is the process of minimizing free energy across all three levels simultaneously.

B.5.2 Why Three Levels Are Necessary

The total free energy \(F = F_1 + F_2 + F_3 + F_{\text{temporal}}\) requires all three levels for full minimization:

B.5.3 The Hard Problem as a Free Energy Problem

Level Absent Consequence Phenomenological Analog
No Level 1 \(F_1\) unconstrained: no interoceptive grounding Depersonalization — experience without felt body
No Level 2 \(F_2\) unconstrained: no schema integration Dreamless sleep — raw affect without structure
No Level 3 \(F_3\) unconstrained: no self-model Minimal consciousness — structured experience without self-awareness
All three Full minimization: coherent self-aware experience Normal waking consciousness

The "explanatory gap" between physical processes and subjective experience corresponds, in this framework, to the gap between:

  1. The objective description: gradient descent on a variational bound, \(\dot{\boldsymbol{\mu}}_l = D\boldsymbol{\mu}_l - \kappa_l \frac{\partial F}{\partial \boldsymbol{\mu}_l}\)
  2. The subjective description: "what it is like" to be the system performing this inference

The RSP model does not claim to close this gap by reduction. Instead, it dissolves the gap by showing that the objective description already has the structure we attribute to subjective experience:

  • Valence = direction of the free energy gradient at Level 1
  • Intentionality = the generative model's predictions (content is what is predicted)
  • Unity = the single scalar \(F\) integrating all levels
  • Selfhood = the recursive fixed point \(\boldsymbol{\mu}_3^{\text{rec}}\)
  • Temporal flow = the temporal prediction errors \(\boldsymbol{\eta}_l\) and predicted future \(\hat{\mathbf{e}}(t+1)\)

These are not merely analogies. If one accepts the functionalist premise that consciousness is constituted by its relational and structural properties — a substantive philosophical position defended in the paper body (§VIII) — then these correspondences are structural identities: the mathematical properties of free energy minimization in a three-level recursive hierarchy are the properties we require of consciousness.

B.6 Learning: Long-Term Free Energy Minimization

The preceding analysis characterizes consciousness at a single moment — the phenomenal state at convergence of the free energy dynamics. We now turn to how the free energy landscape itself changes over time through learning, asking how the generative model's parameters and structure are shaped by experience.

B.6.1 Parameter Learning

The generative model parameters \(\boldsymbol{\theta} = \{\mathbf{W}_l, \mathbf{b}_l, \mathbf{W}_{\text{int}}, \mathbf{W}_{\mathcal{M}}\}\) are updated on a slower timescale by gradient descent on expected free energy:

$$\dot{\boldsymbol{\theta}} = -\kappa_{\theta} \cdot \left\langle \frac{\partial F}{\partial \boldsymbol{\theta}} \right\rangle_{\tau}$$

where \(\langle \cdot \rangle_{\tau}\) denotes averaging over a time window \(\tau\) (minutes to hours). This corresponds to synaptic plasticity — the slow adjustment of connection weights that shapes the generative model.

B.6.2 Model Selection and Cultural Learning

Over developmental timescales (months to years), the system selects among competing generative model structures by minimizing the expected free energy of the model itself:

$$m^* = \arg\min_m \; \mathbb{E}\big[F_m\big]$$

This implements the RSP model's claim that conceptual categories \(\mathcal{C}\) are culturally learned: different cultures provide different generative models for categorizing affect, and the child adopts the model that best predicts their social environment's responses. The free energy framework explains why emotional concepts differ across cultures — each culture's model is locally optimal for its particular pattern of social contingencies.

B.6.3 Hierarchical Learning Rates

A key feature of the RSP free energy landscape is that learning rates differ by level:

Level Timescale Learning Rate What Changes
Level 1 Milliseconds–seconds \(\kappa_1 \gg \kappa_2 \gg \kappa_3\) Interoceptive expectations (fast)
Level 2 Seconds–minutes \(\kappa_2\) Schema configurations (moderate)
Level 3 Minutes–hours \(\kappa_3\) Self-model, emotional concepts (slow)
Parameters Hours–years \(\kappa_{\theta}\) Synaptic weights (very slow)
Model structure Years–lifetime — Conceptual repertoire (developmental)

This hierarchy of timescales ensures stability: fast lower-level updates don't destabilize slow upper-level representations, while upper-level changes propagate gradually downward through the generative model. Disruptions to this timescale separation (e.g., trauma rapidly rewriting the self-model) produce pathological states.

B.7 Expected Free Energy and Planning

B.7.1 Active Inference with Temporal Depth

The system doesn't just minimize current free energy — it minimizes expected free energy over a planning horizon \(T\):

$$G(\pi) = \sum_{\tau=t}^{t+T} \mathbb{E}_{q(\mathbf{y}_{\tau}, \boldsymbol{\theta} | \pi)}\big[F(\mathbf{y}_{\tau}, \boldsymbol{\theta})\big]$$

where \(\pi\) is a policy (sequence of planned actions) and the expectation is over predicted future observations and states under that policy. This decomposes into:

$$G(\pi) = \underbrace{-\sum_{\tau} \mathbb{E}_{q}\big[\ln p(\mathbf{y}_{\tau})\big]}_{\text{pragmatic value (reward)}} - \underbrace{\sum_{\tau} \mathbb{E}_{q}\big[D_{\text{KL}}[q(\boldsymbol{\theta}|\mathbf{y}_{\tau}) \| q(\boldsymbol{\theta})]\big]}_{\text{epistemic value (information gain)}}$$

The first term drives the system toward predicted observations that are consistent with its preferences (homeostasis, positive valence). The second term drives epistemic foraging — seeking observations that reduce uncertainty about hidden states.

B.7.2 Social Prediction as Expected Free Energy

At Level 3, the planning horizon includes predicted social outcomes. The expected free energy of a social action \(\pi_{\text{social}}\) is:

$$G_3(\pi_{\text{social}}) = \mathbb{E}\bigg[\sum_{d=1}^{D_{\max}} \gamma^d \big\|\mathcal{M}^{(d)}(t+\tau) - \mathcal{M}^{(d-1)}(t+\tau)\big\|_{\boldsymbol{\Pi}_3^{(d)}}^2 \;\bigg|\; \pi_{\text{social}}\bigg]$$

The system chooses social actions that minimize predicted discrepancy between self-model and socially-reflected self-model. This is the free energy formulation of impression management, self-presentation, and social conformity — all driven by the same principle that drives perception and action: minimizing surprise.

B.8 Summary: The Free Energy Landscape of Consciousness

The total free energy functional for the RSP model:

$$\boxed{F = \underbrace{\frac{1}{2}\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_1^T \boldsymbol{\Pi}_1 \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_1}_{F_1:\;\text{interoceptive}} + \underbrace{\frac{1}{2}\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_2^T \boldsymbol{\Pi}_2 \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_2}_{F_2:\;\text{schema}} + \underbrace{\frac{1}{2}\boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_3^T \boldsymbol{\Pi}_3 \boldsymbol{\varepsilon}_3 + F_3^{\text{rec}}}_{F_3:\;\text{recursive self}} + \underbrace{\sum_l \frac{1}{2}\boldsymbol{\eta}_l^T \boldsymbol{\Sigma}_l^{-1} \boldsymbol{\eta}_l}_{F_{\text{temp}}:\;\text{temporal}} - \underbrace{\frac{1}{2}\sum_l \ln|\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l|}_{C:\;\text{complexity}}}$$

The system minimizes \(F\) simultaneously through:

  1. Perception: updating \(\boldsymbol{\mu}_l\) (changing beliefs to match observations)
  2. Action: updating \(\mathbf{u}\) (changing observations to match beliefs)
  3. Attention: updating \(\boldsymbol{\Pi}_l\) (changing confidence to match reliability)
  4. Learning: updating \(\boldsymbol{\theta}\) (changing the generative model)
  5. Planning: selecting \(\pi\) (choosing actions to minimize expected future \(F\))

Consciousness is the state of the hierarchy when all five optimization processes operate together — the felt sense of being an organism that knows itself, predicts its social world, and acts to maintain coherence between its self-model and its place in that world.

References for Appendix B

  • Buckley, C. L., Kim, C. S., McGregor, S., & Seth, A. K. (2017). The free energy principle for action and perception: A mathematical review. Journal of Mathematical Psychology, 81, 55-79.
  • Friston, K. (2005). A theory of cortical responses. Philosophical Transactions of the Royal Society B, 360(1456), 815-836.
